Long live the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEScott1973404_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEScott1973404-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>The Assembly passed a resolution that "With effect from the day following the close of the present session of the Assembly [i.e., April 19], the League of Nations shall cease to exist except for the sole purpose of the liquidation of its affairs as provided in the present resolution."<sup id="cite_ref-Myers_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myers-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>  A Board of Liquidation consisting of nine persons from different countries spent the next 15 months overseeing the transfer of the League\'s assets and functions to the United Nations or specialised bodies, finally dissolving itself on July 31, 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-Myers_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Myers-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The archive of the League of Nations was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">United Nations Office at Geneva</a> and is now an entry in the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Register" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory of the World Register">Memory of the World Register</a>.\n</p><p>In the past few decades, by research using the League Archives at Geneva, historians have reviewed the legacy of the League of Nations as the United Nations has faced similar troubles to those of the interwar period. Current consensus views that, even though the League failed to achieve its ultimate goal of world peace, it did manage to build new roads towards expanding the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> across the globe; strengthened the concept of <a href="/wiki/Collective_security" title="Collective security">collective security</a>, giving a voice to smaller nations; helped to raise awareness to problems like <a href="/wiki/Epidemics" class="mw-redirect" title="Epidemics">epidemics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slavery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labour</a>, colonial tyranny, <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugee crisis</a> and general working conditions through its numerous commissions and committees; and paved the way for new forms of statehood, as the <a href="/wiki/Mandate_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandate system">mandate system</a> put the colonial powers under international observation.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Professor <a href="/wiki/David_M._Kennedy_(historian)" title="David M. Kennedy (historian)">David Kennedy</a> portrays the League as a unique moment when international affairs were "institutionalised", as opposed to the pre\xe2\x80\x93First World War methods of law and politics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedy1987_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedy1987-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The principal Allies in the Second World War (the UK, the USSR, France, the U.S., and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China_(1912%E2%80%9349)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China (1912\xe2\x80\x9349)">Republic of China</a>) became permanent members of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> in 1946. (In 1971 the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People\'s Republic of China</a> replaced the Republic of China (then only in control of <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>) as permanent member of the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Security Council">UN Security Council</a>, and in 1991 the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> replaced the USSR.) Decisions of the Security Council are binding on all members of the UN; unanimous decisions are not required, unlike in the League Council. Permanent members of the Security Council can wield a veto to protect their vital interests.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENorthedge1986278\xe2\x80\x93281_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENorthedge1986278\xe2\x80\x93281-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=League_of_Nations&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
